## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics) — nonlinear/forced oscillators
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration and the only state feature is position x (plus time t), which matches second-order oscillator models where the restoring force is a function of displacement (often nonlinear) and may include explicit time-dependent forcing or parametric stiffness modulation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (Hooke restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small oscillations about a stable equilibrium)
- Shifted equilibrium / gravity bias: dv_dt = -c0 * (x - c1) (oscillation about an offset equilibrium)
- Quadratic nonlinearity (asymmetry): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**2 (non-symmetric potential / bias in restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Cubic-quintic stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 (stronger anharmonicity at large amplitude)
- Pendulum restoring (exact): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) (rotational oscillator / large-angle pendulum)
- Sine-series anharmonic restoring: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * sin(c3 * x) (Fourier-like restoring force in periodic potentials)
- Nonlinear stiffness via absolute value: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * Abs(x) * x (piecewise-linear/soft-contact type stiffness)
- Saturating restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * x / (c1 + x**2) (restoring force weakens at large |x|, bounded acceleration)
- Time-periodic external drive: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3) (forced oscillator with harmonic driving)
- Time-periodic drive with multiple harmonics: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * sin(c2 * t) + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (non-sinusoidal/compound forcing)
- Parametric oscillator (Mathieu-type stiffness modulation): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * x (time-varying stiffness / parametric resonance)
- Parametric Duffing (time-varying linear stiffness + cubic): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * x**3 (parametric excitation with anharmonic spring)
- Time-dependent equilibrium position: dv_dt = -c0 * (x - c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) (moving support / base excitation in displacement form)
- Potential-gradient form (polynomial potential): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * x + c2 * x**2 + c3 * x**3) (generic conservative oscillator where dv_dt = -dV/dx)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: conservative oscillators around x=0 often yield dv_dt as an odd function of x (terms like x, x**3, sin(c*x)); presence of x**2 or constant terms suggests asymmetry or bias.
- Hardening vs softening spring: adding -c1 * x**3 changes frequency with amplitude; c1 > 0 typically hardens (stiffer at large |x|), c1 < 0 softens.
- Bounded acceleration at large |x|: rational forms like -c0 * x / (c1 + x**2) indicate saturation/limiting force (e.g., geometric constraints or nonlinear compliance).
- Large-angle pendulum signature: dv_dt proportional to sin(c*x) (not just x) indicates periodic restoring torque and amplitude-dependent period.
- External driving vs parametric excitation: additive sinusoid in t (e.g., +c*sin(c*t)) indicates direct forcing, while time-dependent coefficients multiplying x (e.g., -(c0+c1*cos(c*t))*x) indicate parametric modulation.
- Moving equilibrium/base excitation: dependence on (x - g(t)) suggests the system is being shaken or the rest length/support position varies in time.
- Multi-harmonic time terms: sums of sin(c*t) at different frequencies imply non-sinusoidal drive or waveform decomposition (Fourier content).
- Equilibrium location from dv_dt=0: solving dv_dt(x,t)=0 reveals stable/unstable points; multiple real roots in x (from cubic/quintic) imply bistability/metastability typical of Duffing-like systems.

**GT numerical expression:**
`-1.99164100804766*x**3 - 1.99164100804766*x*(0.0248350833882069*t + 1) - 1.99164100804766*x + 0.799842060559254*sin(t)`

Let me simplify the GT:
- `-1.99164100804766*x**3` → x³ term
- `-1.99164100804766*x*(0.0248350833882069*t + 1)` = `-1.99164100804766*0.0248350833882069*t*x - 1.99164100804766*x` → t*x term and x term
- `-1.99164100804766*x` → another x term
- `0.799842060559254*sin(t)` → sin(t) term

Combining x terms: `-1.99164100804766*x - 1.99164100804766*x` = `-3.98328201609532*x`

So GT = **A*x + B*x³ + C*t*x + D*sin(t)** where A, B, C, D are specific constants.

GT has exactly these basis functions: **x, x³, t*x, sin(t)**

Now I'll check each candidate for structural equivalence (can it reduce to exactly these 4 basis functions?).

Note: `sin(t)` can be written as `cos(t + c)` with appropriate phase shift, so `cos(c + t)` with free c is equivalent to a scaled sin(t).

Let me systematically go through candidates:

**Candidate 1:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*x**3 + c7*t*x`
Has cos(c2+t) ≡ sin(t) ✓, but also sin(c4*t+c5) which is an extra sinusoidal. Set c3=0 to eliminate it. Then: x, cos(c2+t), x³, t*x → **MATCH**

**Candidate 2:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*sin(c6*t + c7) + c8*t*x`
Two sin terms, set one to zero. Remaining: x, x³, sin(c*t+c), t*x. Need c3=1 for sin(t). **MATCH**

**Candidate 3:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*sin(c6 + c7*t) + c8*t*x + c9`
Extra constant c9 and two sins. Set c5=0, c9=0. Then: x, x³, sin(c3*t+c4), t*x with c3=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 4:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x/(c5*t + c6) + c7/(c5*t + c6) + c8*t*x`
Has x³ missing, has rational terms in t. The rational terms x/(at+b) and 1/(at+b) cannot produce x³. Set c3=0, c7=0 → no x³ term. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 5:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x/(c4*x + c5) + c6/(c4*x + c5) + c7*x**3 + c8*t*x`
Has rational terms in x. Set c3=0, c6=0 to eliminate them. Then: x, cos(c2+t), x³, t*x. **MATCH**

**Candidate 6:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*log(c4*t + 1) + c5*x**3 + c6*t*x`
Has log term. Set c3=0. Then: x, cos(c2+t), x³, t*x. **MATCH**

**Candidate 7:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x**3 + c4*t*x + c5*x + c6`
c5*x merges with c0*x, c6 is constant. Set c6=0. Then: (c0+c5)*x, cos, x³, t*x. **MATCH**

**Candidate 8:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x**3 + c4*t*x + c5`
Extra constant c5. Set c5=0. Then: x, cos, x³, t*x. **MATCH**

**Candidate 9:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x**3 + c4*t*x + c5*t + c6`
Extra t term and constant. Set c5=0, c6=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 10:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x**3 + c4*t/(c5*t + c6) + c7/(c5*t + c6) + c8*t*x`
Rational terms in t. Set c4=0, c7=0. Then: x, cos, x³, t*x. **MATCH**

**Candidate 11:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3 + c4*t) + c5*exp(c6*t) + c7*t*x + c8`
Set c5=0, c8=0, c4=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 12:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x**3 + c4*t/(c5*x + c6) + c7*t*x + c8/(c5*x + c6)`
Rational terms in x: t/(ax+b) and 1/(ax+b). These cannot be zeroed independently unless c4=0 and c8=0. Set both to 0. Then: x, cos, x³, t*x. **MATCH**

**Candidate 13:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x**3 + c4*t*x + c5*t*(c6 + x)**c7`
The term c5*t*(c6+x)^c7 is complex. Set c5=0. Then: x, cos, x³, t*x. **MATCH**

**Candidate 14:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x**c4 + c5*t*(c6 + x)**c7`
Need x³ → set c4=3. Need t*x → set c7=1, then c5*t*(c6+x) = c5*c6*t + c5*t*x. The c5*c6*t term is extra (pure t). GT has no pure t term. Can't eliminate it without losing t*x. Unless c6=0, then c5*t*x. But then no constant x term offset... wait, we have c0*x + c3*x³ + c5*t*x + cos term. We need the coefficient of x to match GT. This works if c6=0. Then: c0*x + cos + x³ + t*x. But GT needs a specific ratio between x and t*x coefficients - that's fine with free constants. **MATCH**

**Candidate 15:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*t + c4*x**3 + c5*t*x`
Extra t term. Set c3=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 16:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*exp(c4*x) + c5*x**3 + c6*t*x`
Set c3=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 17:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x + c4*x**3 + c5*t*x`
(c0+c3)*x + cos + x³ + t*x. **MATCH**

**Candidate 18:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x**3 + c4*t*x`
Exactly: x, cos(c2+t), x³, t*x. **MATCH**

**Candidate 19:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x + c4*x**3 + (c5+c6)*t*x`
Same as 17. **MATCH**

**Candidate 20:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x**3 + c4*t*x + c5*x*(c6 + t)**c7`
Set c5=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 21:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x**c4 + c5*x*(c6 + t)**c7`
Set c4=3 for x³. c5*x*(c6+t)^c7: set c7=1 → c5*x*(c6+t) = c5*c6*x + c5*x*t. The c5*c6*x merges with c0*x. So: (c0+c5*c6)*x + cos + x³ + c5*t*x. **MATCH**

**Candidate 22:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*t**c3 + c4*sin(c5 + c6*t) + c7*t*x + c8`
Set c2=0, c8=0, c6=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 23:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*t**c4 + c5*x**3 + c6*t*x`
Set c3=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 24:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*x**3 + c6*t*x`
Set c3=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 25:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*log(c4*x + 1) + c5*x**3 + c6*t*x`
Set c3=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 26:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*t/(c6*x + c7) + c8/(c6*x + c7) + c9*t*x`
Set c5=0, c8=0, c3=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 27:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x**c4 + c5*x**3 + c6*t*x`
Set c3=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 28:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*log(c6*t + 1) + c7*t*x`
Set c5=0, c3=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 29:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3 + c4*t) + c5*x*(c6 + t)**c7 + c8*t*x + c9`
Set c5=0, c9=0, c4=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 30:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*t*x + c6*x + c7`
Set c7=0, c3=1. (c0+c6)*x + x³ + sin(t) + t*x. **MATCH**

**Candidate 31:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3 + c4*t) + c5*t*x + c6`
Set c6=0, c4=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 32:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3 + c4*t) + c5*x + (c6+c7)*t*x + c8`
Set c8=0, c4=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 33:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*t/(c6*t + c7) + c8/(c6*t + c7) + c9*t*x`
Set c5=0, c8=0, c3=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 34:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*t*x + c6*t + c7`
Set c6=0, c7=0, c3=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 35:** Set c5=0, c9=0, c4=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 59:** `c0*x + c1*x*cos(c2*t + c3) + c4*x**c5 + c6*sin(c7*t + c8)`
The term c1*x*cos(c2*t+c3) is x*cos(...). GT needs t*x, not x*cos(t). These are different basis functions. Can't set c1*x*cos = t*x. Set c1=0 → lose t*x term entirely. **NO MATCH**
